<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-medicine">GENERAL MEDICINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-medicine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-2-definition-of-terms-used-in-medicine">3.2 DEFINITION OF TERMS USED IN MEDICINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-definition-of-terms-used-in-medicine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Medicine</strong>: Is the science and or practice that involves treating diseases using external treatment or remedies as opposed to mechanical and operational procedures (use of non-surgical methods).</p>
<p>Is the science and or practice of the diagnosis, treatment and prevention of diseases</p>
<p><strong>Health</strong>: Is the state of complete wellbeing of a person mentally, physically, socially and spiritually and not merely in the absence of a disease.</p>
<p><strong>Etiology</strong>: Is the study of disease causation.</p>
<p><strong>Pathology</strong>: Is the study of the course of disease or disease process and the structures that are involved.</p>
<p><strong>Symptoms</strong>: Are the complaints of the patients about any presenting condition or disease.</p>
<p><strong>Signs</strong>: Are features that are seen by the naked eyes on the patient</p>
<p><strong>Physical signs</strong>: Are ones discovered on physical examination</p>
<p><strong>Complications</strong>: Are those signs, symptoms lesions or diseases that may result from an original disease.</p>
<p><strong>Syndrome</strong>: It’s a combination of signs and symptoms that form a distinct clinical picture indicative of a particular disorder.</p>
<p><strong>Diagnosis</strong>: Is the process of determining the nature of a disorder by considering the patient’s signs and symptoms, medical background, results of laboratory tests and radiological examinations.</p>
<p><strong>Differential diagnosis</strong>: Is the knowledge of other diseases which resemble the disease that the patient is suspected to be having and the point of difference which help in giving the final conclusion.</p>
<p><strong>Disease</strong>: Is a disorder with specific causes and recognizable signs and symptoms.</p>
<p><strong>Prophylaxis</strong>: Is any means taken to prevent a disease like immunization, hygiene chemotherapy etc.</p>
<p><strong>Prognosis</strong>: Is an assessment of the future course and outcomes of a patient’s disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-causes-of-diseases">GENERAL CAUSES OF DISEASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-causes-of-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<ul>
<li>Congenital</li>
<li>Idiopathic</li>
<li>Hereditary</li>
<li>Allergic reaction</li>
<li>Microorganisms</li>
<li>Metabolic disorders</li>
<li>Injury</li>
<li>Endocrine disorders</li>
<li>Degeneration causes</li>
<li>Nutritional deficiency</li>
<li>Immune system disorders</li>
<li>Iatrogenic causes</li>
<li>Abnormal cell multiplication</li>
</ul>
<p>Congenital causes: This is when someone is born with an abnormality. It mainly occurs during intra-uterine life. It may be due to infections of the mother, certain drugs including native medicine, x-ray.</p>
<p>Examples include: Hare lip and cleft palate, congenital heart disease.</p>
<p>Idiopathic: Is when the exact cause of disease is unknown like some cancers, epilepsy, mental disorders etc.</p>
<p>Hereditary: This is when a disease is transmitted from parents to their off springs (children) like sickle cell disease, hemophilia etc.</p>
<p>Allergic disorders: This is when someone reacts with physical symptoms and signs to normal substances which other people do not react to. The allergens may be inhaled, injected into tissue or direct contact to grass, fumes, powder or ingested e.g. Asthma skin diseases, anaphylactic shock etc.</p>
<p>Injury: It is a physical harm to a person.</p>
<p>Microorganisms: The disease may be brought about by bacteria, viruses, fungi, parasites, protozoa etc. like measles, malaria, pneumonia etc.</p>
<p>Metabolic disorders: This is when the body is unable to deal with certain elements of the diet or complex organic constituents of the body resulting into their accumulation in the body thus becoming dangerous in the body. E.g. DM, Mental confusion, hyperlipidemia, hypocalcaemia, etc.</p>
<p>Endocrine disorders: This is when over secretion or under secretion of hormones may alter various activities in the body like thyrotoxicosis, acromegaly.</p>
<p>Nutritional deficiency: This is when lack of essential nutrients in the body like proteins, vitamins, minerals like iron results into certain conditions like marasmus, anemia, kwashiorkor etc.</p>
<p>Abnormal cell multiplication: This may lead to tumors and or cancers. The reason for their multiplication may not be known.</p>
<p>Degeneration: This is the deterioration and loss of specialized function of a tissue or organ. This is common in advanced age e.g. Osteoarthritis, dementia, osteoporosis etc.</p>
<p>Iatrogenic: Iatrogenic condition or disease is one that has resulted from treatment or care of another disease. This can be surgical or medical treatment or care. E.g. Aspiration pneumonia, pressure sores, DVT etc.</p>
<p>Disorders of immune system:</p>
<p>When the immune system is compromised especially in children and elderly, various conditions or diseases set in.</p>
<p>LEVELS OF DISEASE PREVENTION</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diseases-of-the-cardiovascular-system-heart-and-blood-vessels-review-of-the-anatomy-and-physiology-of-the-system-first">DISEASES OF THE CARDIOVASCULAR SYSTEM, HEART AND BLOOD VESSELS ((review of the anatomy and physiology of the system first)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diseases-of-the-cardiovascular-system-heart-and-blood-vessels-review-of-the-anatomy-and-physiology-of-the-system-first" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>HEART DISEASE:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Refers to the pathological condition of the heart i.e. the heart is imperfect either in structure, function or both.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-heart-disease">Causes of heart disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-heart-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rheumatic fever- Leads to the narrowing of the heart valves causing obstruction of the blood flow within the heart, backflow of blood thus insufficiency of the heart function.</p>
<p>Congenital abnormalities- heart disease occurs during growth and development of the heart during intra-uterine life (pregnancy) especially in 1st and 2nd trimester.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>3</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Syphilis-this causes aortic dilatation and aortic contraction which narrows it and causes backflow.</p>
<p>Hypertension-in hypertension, blood vessels hardens and narrows and this causes cardiac overload so as to pump blood through the narrowed arteries.</p>
<p>Infections- in acute infections, toxins may affect the heart muscles e.g. in typhoid fever, tonsillitis, pharyngitis etc.</p>
<p>Chronic lung disease-heart disease which is secondary to lung condition is called Cor-pulmonale. Lung conditions like lung cancer, chronic bronchitis, lung abscess, and pleural effusion.</p>
<p>Thyrotoxicosis- this leads to increased metabolism due to increased tissue demand thus the heart has to work harder to meet tissues demand</p>
<p>Anaemia-In anaemia the heart itself is not receiving enough oxygenated blood and necessary factors to enable it pump blood properly. The heart muscle becomes and eventually fails.</p>
<p>Alcoholism and smoking- alcohol weakens the heart muscles (this is called alcoholic cardiopathy). In smokers cigarette contains nicotine which constricts/narrows the blood vessels leading to hypertension.</p>
<p>Malnutrition-this leads to nutritional cardiopathy as a result of lack essential nutrients thus making the heart muscles weak.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-heart-disease">Signs and symptoms heart disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-heart-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Chest pain-this is the most common symptom. The pain varies according to condition like retrosternal heavy or gripping sensation with radiations to the left arm or neck provoked by exertion and relieved by rest especially in angina pectoris.</li>
<li>Dyspnoea (breathlessness)- this is due to oedema of the alveoli and pulmonary interstitial, dyspnoea may be orthopnea, paroxysmal nocturnal dyspnoea.</li>
<li>Palpitations- this is increased awareness of the heart beat or feeling of slow, rapid or irregular heartbeats/ rhythms.</li>
<li>Syncope-this is temporary transient loss of consciousness due to inadequate blood flow to the brain.</li>
<li>Fatigue-this is due to inadequate systemic perfusion</li>
<li>Peripheral oedema-due to salt and water retention brought about renal under perfusion and consequent activation of the Rennin Angiotensin Aldosterone System (RAAS)</li>
<li>Clubbing of the fingers</li>
<li>Cyanosis</li>
<li>Irregular thread pulse</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Raised jugular venous pressure and extended jugular veins.</li>
<li>Restlessness and irritability</li>
<li>On auscultation heart murmurs are heard.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations-done-in-heart-disease">Investigations done in heart disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations-done-in-heart-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inflammatory-disorders-of-the-heart-and-blood-vessels">INFLAMMATORY DISORDERS OF THE HEART AND BLOOD VESSELS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inflammatory-disorders-of-the-heart-and-blood-vessels" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rheumatic-fever">RHEUMATIC FEVER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rheumatic-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Is an inflammatory disease that affects the connective tissues particularly the heart, joints, muscles and skin.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>In the cardiovascular system, it is an inflammatory disease of the heart potentially involving all layers of the heart. This is known as rheumatic heart disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The exact cause is unknown; however rheumatic fever appears 2-3 weeks after a streptococcal infection in boils, tonsillitis, pharyngitis, sore throat.</p>
<p>The streptococcal infection is particularly caused by group A Beta haemolytic streptococci</p>
<p>Rheumatic fever is mainly found in children (5-15 years) and also in young adults.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rheumatic fever occurs after 2-3 weeks of group A Beta hemolytic streptococcal infection of upper respiratory tract infections like tonsillitis, pharyngitis, sore throat etc. In response to infection antibodies are produced causing immunological or inflammatory responses like irritation, oedema/swelling, pain, redness, heat and loss of function in the affected connective tissues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-rheumatic-fever">Signs and symptoms of rheumatic fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-rheumatic-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sudden onset (10-21 days after sore throat pharyngitis tonsillitis).</li>
<li>Raised body temperature</li>
<li>General malaise and fatigue</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>Chest pain</li>
<li>Abdominal pain</li>
<li>Migratory joint pains and tenderness (especially large joints)</li>
<li>Difficulty in breathing</li>
<li>Swelling, heat, redness and limited movement in knees, ankles, elbow, and shoulder and wrist joints</li>
<li>Subcutaneous nodules and erythema marginatum</li>
<li>Tachycardia, heart murmurs peripheral oedema</li>
<li>Pericardial friction rub on auscultation</li>
<li>Chorea- involuntary, purposeless, rapid movements</li>
<li>On chest x-ray cardiomegaly heart and valves will be seen damaged</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note-rheumatic-fever-bites-the-heart-and-licks-the-joints">NOTE: Rheumatic fever bites the heart and licks the joints<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note-rheumatic-fever-bites-the-heart-and-licks-the-joints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations-and-diagnosis">Investigations and diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations-and-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Diagnosis may be based on symptoms and signs like migratory joint pains, chorea and investigations like:</p>

✓ Blood for complete blood count
✓ Blood for culture and sensitivity
✓ ECG

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims">Aims<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To eradicate the causative microorganism</li>
<li>To relieve pain and fever</li>
<li>To reduce on the cardiac workload</li>
<li>Admit a patient who is in acute phase</li>
<li>Ensure complete bed rest to rest the heart and the joints</li>
<li>Position- preferably sitting up position especially in breathlessness.</li>
<li>Apply a bed cradle to reduce weight or relieve pressure of clothes on the affected joints</li>
<li>Apply warm or cold compresses on the affected joints to relieve pains</li>
<li>Observations- vital observations i.e. Temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure and record them in the patient's file and other observations like conscious levels, oedema and report the findings to the doctor.</li>
<li>History taking- it should be thorough to determine the predisposing causes.</li>
<li>Tepid sponging to reduce on the raised body temperatures.</li>
<li>Inform the DOCTOR to come and re-assesses, re-examines the patient and order for investigations and prescribe treatment/drugs.</li>
<li>Psychotherapy- reassures the patient in order to allay anxiety.</li>
<li>Monitor and balance the fluid balance chart.</li>
<li>Diet- A light diet in acute phase to neutralize the toxins if there is no oedema severe heart involvement. Normal diet is started when the patient recovers from acute phase. It should be highly nutritious with plenty of proteins, vitamins fluids and roughages.</li>
<li>Drug therapy: Analgesics e.g. Aspirin 125-150mg/kg body weight in divided doses in children, 6-8 adults in acute phase in divided doses of 4-6 hours and 8 hourly when the condition improves. Aspirin is a drug of choice in joint pains &amp; a high dose is given.</li>
</ul>
<p>Antibiotics – I.M Benzathine penicillin 1.2-2.4 mega units weekly and prophylactically every 2-4 months until 18 years (if not life time treatment).</p>
<p>Or phenoxymethyl penicillin (Pen V) orally</p>
<p>Or erythromycin or azithromycin 250-500mg if hypersensitive to penicillin</p>
<ul>
<li>Health education on:</li>
<li>Drug compliance to avoid relapses.</li>
</ul>

Patient to avoid strenuous work in order to rest the heart and joints
Encourage oral hygiene and all dental carries must be treated or extracted promptly and prophylactic appropriate antibiotics should be given to prevent infections hence complications.
To seek medical help in case of exaggerated cardiac symptoms like palpitations distended jugular veins, oedema, dyspnoea etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-rheumatic-fever">Complications of rheumatic fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-rheumatic-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

☑ Endocarditis
☑ Myocarditis
☑ Pericarditis
☑ Rheumatic heart disease (RHD)
☑ Renal disease</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rheumatic-heart-disease">RHEUMATIC HEART DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rheumatic-heart-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a chronic condition characterized by scaring and deformity of the heart valves.</p>
<p>It is a complication of rheumatic fever due to poorly treated upper respiratory tract infections like tonsillitis, pharyngitis and dental decays</p>
<p>The sequelae of rheumatic heart disease are found primarily in young adults.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Microorganisms- bacteria mainly group A Beta hemolytic streptococci</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-causes">Predisposing causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Poorly treated URTIS like tonsillitis, pharyngitis</li>
<li>Dental carries</li>
<li>Boils</li>
<li>Overcrowded and poorly ventilated situations</li>
<li>Social-economic factors –common among poor</li>
<li>May be a familial tendency (-auto-immune RF)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note">NOTE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rheumatic fever episodes are marked by carditis and affect all the layers of the heart (endocardium, myocardium, and pericardium). This generalized involvement is called rheumatic pancarditis (perimyocarditis)</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Rheumatic endocarditis:</p>
<p>Affects the valves</p>
<p>It’s characterized by swelling and erosion of the valve leaflets. As a result vegetation form from deposits of fibrin and blood cells in the area of erosion.</p>
<p>The lesions create fibrous thickening of the valve leaflets, fusion of commissures and chordate tendinae and fibrosis of papillary muscles resulting into Val volar stenosis. Inability of the heart valves to move leads to regurgitation.</p>
<p>The mitral and aortic valves are affected most.</p>
<p>Rheumatic Myocarditis:</p>
<p>This is characterized by nodules which are formed by a reaction to inflammation with swelling and fragmentation of collagen fibres. These nodules are called ASCOFF’S BODIES</p>
<p>As the nodules age, they become more fibrous and scar tissue is formed in the myocardium leading to heart failure.</p>
<p>Rheumatic Pericarditis:</p>
<p>Affects both layers of the pericardium which become thickened and covered with a fibrous exudates. When healing occurs fibrosis and adhesions develop that partially or completely obliterate the pericardial sac.</p>
<p>Clinical presentation of rheumatic heart disease</p>
<ul>
<li>Dyspnoea</li>
<li>Palpitations from atrial fibrillation</li>
<li>Fatigue and general body weakness</li>
<li>Haemoptysis</li>
<li>Chest pain</li>
<li>Activity intolerance</li>
<li>Syncope</li>
<li>Pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>Heart murmurs on auscultation</li>
</ul>
<p>Investigation and diagnosis</p>
<p>Diagnosis is based on clinical signs and symptoms and it’s confirmed by investigations.</p>
<p>Investigations</p>

<p>✓ Thorough history taking- History of streptococcal infections like tonsillitis, pharyngitis, dental decay
✓ Physical examination from head to toe
✓ Chest x-ray
✓ Electrocardiogram (measures patterns of electric impulses generated by heart rhythms)
✓ Echocardiogram (uses sound waves to check the structure of your heart)
✓ Cardiac catheterization</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aims">Aims:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>To restore normal cardiac function</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To improve activity tolerance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To help patient understand the disease process and to prevent disease re-occurrence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Admit patient in a well-ventilated and quiet room.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure complete bed rest.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Position- sitting up position to aid breathing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reassure patient to allay anxiety.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observations- vital observations temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure initially hourly the 2 hourly until patient’s conditions improves. Respiration and pulse may be monitored more frequently. Observe also for patient’s conscious levels, signs of shock, oedema cyanosis etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inform DOCTOR who will re –examines the patient and order for investigations and prescribe drugs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diet- provide a light diet with low or no salt and fat content, provide plenty of vitamins starch and vegetables to ease digestion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Restrict fluids in pulmonary and peripheral oedema.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give small but frequent foods.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drug therapy: the DR will prescribe the following drugs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prophylactic antibiotic therapy in rheumatic fever and infective endocarditis (antibiotics as in rheumatic fever treatment).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Digitalis-digoxin 0.25mg-9.75mg once a day when the pulse is &gt;60 b/m</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diuretics –like furosemide 20-40 mg 2-3 times a day, max 80 mg to relieve oedema.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nitrates- like glyceryl trinitrate 0.3-1mg sub-lingual.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anticoagulants-like aspirin 75-150mg max 300mg, warfarin 5-7mg, max 15 mg (after determining the clotting and the bleeding time).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-interventions">Surgical interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Valvoplasty</p>
<p>Valvotomy</p>
<p>Valve replacement</p>
<p>NB: the rest of the management and nursing care is the same as for patient with rheumatic fever and cardiac failure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pericarditis">PERICARDITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pericarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the inflammation of the pericardium</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pericarditis usually occurs as a complication of other diseases. These include,</p>
<ul>
<li>Acute rheumatism</li>
<li>Infections like viral infections (mumps, HIV, herpes viruses), bacterial infections (streptococci, staphylococci, pneumococci, meningococcal, Haemophilus influenza), fungal infections (like Candida,)</li>
<li>Post myocardial infarction.</li>
<li>Malignant disorders- tumors of the heart (mesothelioma), metastatic Pericarditis due to breast and lung cancer, leukemia.</li>
<li>Excess blood urea (uremic) Pericarditis</li>
<li>Auto-immunity.</li>
<li>Post-surgical procedures of the heart.</li>
<li>Post radiations- chest x-rays.</li>
<li>Familial tendencies.</li>
<li>Idiopathic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-pericarditis">Types of Pericarditis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-pericarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two main types i.e.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-pericarditis">Acute Pericarditis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-pericarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is due to fibrous material being deposited into the pericardial space which can be dry with fibrous scars or wet with effusion.</p>
<p>It is caused by acute rheumatism, infections, myocardial infarction.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>8</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chronic-or-constrictive-pericarditis">Chronic or constrictive Pericarditis;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-or-constrictive-pericarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This may fall acute Pericarditis or rheumatoid disease, TB, haemo-pericardium, and bacterial infections.</p>
<p>As a result, the pericardium becomes thick, fibrous and calcified (fibrous Pericarditis).</p>
<p>If the pericardium becomes inelastic that it interferes with the diastolic filling of the heart, this is called constrictive Pericarditis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note">NOTE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Collection of fluids within the potential space of the serous pericardial sac is called pericardial effusion. When large volumes of pericardial serous fluid collects in the pericardial space, causing ventricular filling to be compromised leading to embarrassment of the circulation is known as cardiac tamponed</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations-of-pericarditis">Clinical manifestations of Pericarditis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations-of-pericarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The onset is sudden with pericardial chest pain.</li>
<li>The pain is central and sharp exacerbated by movement, swallowing, and respiration and lying down. It radiates to the shoulders and neck.</li>
<li>High body temperatures (in infections)</li>
<li>Rapid pulse</li>
<li>Difficulty in breathing—due to pericardial fluid compression</li>
<li>Fatigue and general body weakness due to reduced cardiac output</li>
<li>Increased jugular pressure</li>
<li>Increased or decreased BP</li>
<li>Cough</li>
<li>Ascites and oedema—due to systemic venous congestion</li>
<li>Decreased urine output—due to reduced cardiac output</li>
<li>On auscultation, a pericardial friction rub will be heard</li>
<li>On chest x-ray, pericardial effusion and cardiac tamponed will be seen</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acute Pericarditis usually subsides, however in constrictive Pericarditis life is in danger unless the condition is relieved by surgery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>History taking and general physical examination of patient from head to toe.</li>
<li>Blood for culture and sensitivity</li>
<li>Blood for complete blood count, HB</li>
</ul>

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Chest x-ray.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Pericardio-centesis
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Pericardial biopsy
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> ECG and Electrocardiogram</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims">Aims:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>To treat the underlying cause</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To restore the normal cardiac function.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To prevent complications.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Admit patient in a well-ventilated and quiet room.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure complete bed rest in order to rest the heart and the mind</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reassure patient and patient’s relatives to allay anxiety.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Apply a bed cradle in rheumatic Pericarditis to reduce pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maintain a sitting up position in dyspnoea to aid breathing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observations- vital observations, temperature, pulse, respirations and blood pressure. Pulse is monitored and taken 4 hourly, take and record the sleeping pulse. All the findings must be recorded and any deviations are reported to the senior staff or doctor. Other vital signs like conscious levels, signs of shock, oedema, cyanosis etc. must be observed for.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inform Dr about the patient’s condition.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diet- initially a light diet with low salt intake with plenty of vitamins, starch, proteins and vegetables. Give these feeds in small amount but frequently</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Restrict fluids, salts and fats especially in Ascites and oedema.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drug therapy:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Doctor will prescribe drugs like;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analgesics-aspirin 150-300mg three times a day or indomethacin or ibuprofen 200-400mg three times a day to relieve pericardial chest pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antibiotics- oral penicillin like penv 250-500mg four times a day for 1 week to treat infections, anti-TB drug if patient has TB, Antifungal agents in case of fungal infections.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Corticosteroids- like prednisolone or hydrocortisone to reduce inflammatory response (do not give steroids in known auto-immune cases).</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-managements">Other managements:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-managements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pericardio-centesis- to drain the excess pericardial fluids in order to relieve pressure on to the lungs and heart.</li>
<li>In chronic constrictive Pericarditis, percardiectomy is suggestive (only in non-tuberculosis patients)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diseases-of-the-myocardium">DISEASES OF THE MYOCARDIUM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diseases-of-the-myocardium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="myocarditis">MYOCARDITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myocarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the inflammation of the myocardium</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Idiopathic</li>
<li>Infections like: viral infections (adenovirus, cytomegalo virus, influenza, hepatitis, HIV.), bacterial infections (streptococci-most commonly rheumatic carditis, diphtheria-causes toxic-mediated heart block), fungal infections, Spirochetes- Lyme disease,</li>
<li>Toxins: drugs like penicillins, sulphonamides, anti-TB agents, methyldopa- as these causes hypersensitivity reactions.</li>
<li>Radiations</li>
<li>Autoimmune</li>
<li>Alcohol</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-myocarditis">Signs and Symptoms of Myocarditis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-myocarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Initially it is asymptomatic if the inflammation is limited focal</li>
<li>Later:</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Palpitations</li>
<li>Chest Pains</li>
<li>Dyspnoea</li>
<li>Fainting Attacks</li>
<li>Tachycardia</li>
<li>On Auscultation, at board heart sound, friction rub sound will be hear</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is always good, the patient recovers in 10-20 days but is may cause death if associated with diphtheria.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims">Aims:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="as-in-pericarditis">As in Pericarditis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#as-in-pericarditis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Admit patient in acute phase with exaggerated signs and symptoms. It should be a well-ventilated medical ward</li>
<li>☑ Ensure complete bed rest in order to rest the diseased heart.</li>
<li>☑ The rest of the management is the same as that bin cardiac failure.i.e.</li>
<li>☑ Avoid strenuous exercises for about 6 months</li>
<li>☑ Advise on the cardiac diet.</li>
<li>☑ Drug therapy -Diuretics e.g. Beta blockers, ace inhibitors.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="digitalis">-Digitalis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#digitalis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chronic-cardiomyopathy">CHRONIC CARDIOMYOPATHY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-cardiomyopathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Cardiomyopathies</strong>: are a group of diseases of the myocardium that affect the mechanical or electrical function of the heart.</p>
<p>These are frequently genetic or may be secondary to toxins, endomyocarditis, and autoimmune nutritional deficiencies.</p>
<p><strong>Cardiomyopathies can be classified as</strong>:</p>
<p><strong>Hypertrophic cardiomyopathy (HCM)</strong>: this produces hypertrophy of the myocardium causing thickening of ventricular septum leading to obstruction of blood out flow from the left ventricles.</p>
<p><strong>Dilated cardiomyopathy</strong>: characterized by dilatation of the ventricular chambers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>❖ Chest pains</li>
<li>❖ Dyspnoea</li>
<li>❖ Cardiac arrhythmias</li>
<li>❖ Oedema</li>
<li>❖ Rapid thread pulse</li>
</ul>
