<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention">PREVENTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Quitting smoking
☑ Eating health food
☑ Maintaining a healthy weight
☑ Checking and maintaining a healthy blood pressure
☑ Checking and maintaining healthy cholesterol and blood sugar levels</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>History taking about the family and personal life</li>
<li>Blood tests for cholesterol and glucose level</li>
<li>Electrocardiogram</li>
<li>Exercise stress test echocardiogram</li>
<li>Imaging tests (magnetic resonance angiogram)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Drugs</p>
<p>Use blood thinners like aspirin to minimize clot formation</p>
<p>Blood pressure medications should be taken in case of hypertension</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specific-nursing-care">SPECIFIC NURSING CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Stop smoking as this damage the arteries
☑ Do regular exercises to improve on blood flow
☑ Eat healthy diet i.e foods with low fat and cholesterol levels
☑ Manage stress effectively
☑ Manage any other chronic illness effectively</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pulmonary-embolism">PULMONARY EMBOLISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pulmonary-embolism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It’s a collection matter (solid, liquid or air) that enters the Venus circulation and lodges in the pulmonary vessel</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="riskfactors-for-vte-pe-venous-thrombotic-embolism">RISKFACTORS FOR VTE/PE (VENOUS THROMBOTIC EMBOLISM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#riskfactors-for-vte-pe-venous-thrombotic-embolism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Prolonged immobility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Central venous catheters</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Surgery</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Obesity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advancing age</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Conditions that increase blood clotting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>History of thrombo- embolism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Estrogen therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Heart failure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stroke</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cancer</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>NOTE</p>
<p>The embolus formed may be of</p>
<ul>
<li>Fat/oil</li>
<li>Air</li>
<li>Tumour</li>
<li>Amniotic fluid</li>
</ul>
<p>Foreign bodies e.g. broken IV catheters</p>
<p>Injected particles</p>
<p>SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS</p>
<ul>
<li>Sudden onset</li>
<li>Dyspnea</li>
<li>Sharp stabbing chest pain inspiration</li>
<li>Restlessness</li>
<li>Cough</li>
<li>Haemoptysis</li>
</ul>
<p>OTHER SIGNS INCLUDE</p>
<ul>
<li>oxygen Crackles</li>
<li>Tachypnea</li>
<li>Pleural friction</li>
<li>Diaphoresis</li>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>Petechiae over chest and axillae</li>
<li>Decreased arterial circulation</li>
</ul>
<p>MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>AIMS; to allay anxiety</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>To restore the normal oxygen circulation</p>
<ul>
<li>Admit the patient on a medical ward</li>
<li>Asses the patient for respiration to rule out decreased gas exchange, difficulty in breathing, Pleuritic chest pain, haemoptysis due to pulmonary infarction, cyanosis etc</li>
<li>Position the patient in the most comfortable position</li>
<li>Reassure the patients and her relatives to allay anxiety</li>
<li>Take all the vital observations that is BP/TPR</li>
<li>Call the doctor who will reassess the patient, order for investigations and prescribe the drugs accordingly</li>
<li>The investigations done include;</li>
<li>Computed tomography pulmonary angiography (CT—PA)</li>
<li>Chest x-ray</li>
<li>Doppler ultra sound used to document presence of VTE</li>
<li>Specific management</li>
<li>Administer oxygen using a nasal cannula or mask</li>
<li>Place the patient in a high fowler’s position</li>
<li>Asses the level of oxygen circulation continuously with pulse oximeter</li>
<li>Asses the respiratory status at least 1/2 hourly listen to the lung sounds, ease of respiration should be noted, check the skin colour and capillary refill</li>
<li>Check the cardiac status, BP, distension of neck veins</li>
<li>Do investigations</li>
<li>Examine the throat for presence of Petechiae</li>
<li>Administer prescribed anticoagulants i.e heparin sodium 5000-10000 units bolus, then adjust to 1300 units /hour</li>
<li>Warfarin sodium 10-15 mg orally o.d 3/7 initially then 5-10 mg od</li>
<li>Asses for bleeding</li>
<li>Handle the patient gently</li>
<li>Does the health education about hygiene, the disease process etc</li>
</ul>
<p>DO THE GENERAL NURSING CARE</p>
<p>CORONARY ARTERY DISEASES</p>
<p>Coronary thrombosis/ occlusion</p>
<p>Coronary thrombosis:</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This is the formation of blood clot (thrombus) in the coronary artery, resulting into coronary occlusion.</p>
<p>Coronary occlusion: this refers to the obstruction of the normal flow of blood through the coronary artery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-coronary-occlusion">Causes of Coronary Occlusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-coronary-occlusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Thrombosis - formation of a blood clot in a coronary artery</li>
<li>Embolism - dislodgement of an embolus (blood clot, fat, air, amniotic fluid, foreign body, or microorganism) such that it gets lodged in the coronary artery.</li>
<li>Infections or inflammation of the coronary blood vessels (vasculitis/ arteritis).</li>
<li>Arteriosclerosis.</li>
<li>Atherosclerosis - formation of fatty plagues in the inner walls of the arteries.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertension.</li>
<li>DM.</li>
<li>Cigarette smoking.</li>
<li>Obesity.</li>
<li>High cholesterol diet.</li>
<li>Sedentary life style.</li>
<li>Stress.</li>
<li>Limited exercises.</li>
<li>Race - common in western countries.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any of the above causes results into narrowing of the lumen of the artery leading to stasis of blood flow which predispose to formation of more clots partially or completely hence causing coronary occlusion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-coronary-occlusion">Signs and symptoms of coronary occlusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-coronary-occlusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Onset is sudden.</li>
<li>Sudden painful pressure felt in the upper part of the chest occasionary radiating to the arm, throat or back.</li>
<li>Sudden severe headache</li>
<li>Nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>Profuse sweating.</li>
<li>Pallor.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Anxiety.
Severe dyspnoea with cyanosis.
Fatigue with dizziness.
Loss of balance.
Visual disturbance.
Signs of shock.</p>
<p>NOTE: coronary occlusion/thrombosis is different from angina pectoris in that; coronary occlusion persists for hours or days.</p>
<p>Pain comes at rest not during exertion or exercises.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clinical signs and symptoms</li>
<li>Blood for CBC, RBS.</li>
<li>Echo and electrocardiogram.</li>
<li>Serum cholesterol</li>
<li>CT scan and MRI.</li>
<li>Cardiac catheterization.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Aims:</p>
<ul>
<li>To prevent progression of the disease</li>
<li>To restore the normal coronary circulation</li>
<li>To educate the patient about prevention of the predisposing causes</li>
<li>To prevent complications like heart attack, stroke and death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immediate-care">Immediate care:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immediate-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit patient in a quiet well ventilated room.</li>
<li>Position patient in a sitting up position to aid breathing.</li>
<li>Ensure complete bed rest and loosen all the tight clothing’s</li>
<li>Treat and prevent shock – access and connect I.V fluids and keep the patient warm.</li>
<li>Observations – vital observations and other observations.</li>
<li>Administer oxygen to support respiration and correct cyanosis.</li>
<li>Reassure patient and patient’s relatives and always stay and attend to the patient to allay anxiety.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>35</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Drug therapy:</li>
<li>☑ Administer pain relievers as prescribed by the doctor—morphine 5-15 mg 3-4 times or whenever necessary or cardiac ASA (aspirin) 150-300 mg three times a day.</li>
<li>☑ Adrenaline (epinephrine) 0.1 mg in order to raise blood pressure in case of shock.</li>
<li>☑ Anticoagulants: like heparin I.M./I.V 5000-10000 units for quick effects Oral anticoagulant—warfarin initially 15 mg once a day for 1-2 days then maintenance dose 2.5-7.5 mg once a day, To prevent the extension of the clot and to lessen the chances of embolism.</li>
<li>☑ Thrombolytic/ fibrinolytics like streptokinase, urokinase to break down the clot</li>
<li>☑ Hypotensive: like beta blockers, calcium channel blockers if there is high blood pressure.</li>
</ul>
<p>NOTE: patient on anticoagulants must be monitored for bleeding tendencies. Therefore prothrombin/clotting and bleeding time must be checked before, during and after the therapy.</p>
<p>An antidote for the overdose of heparin is PROTAMINE SULPHATE I.V 1 mg for every 10 units of heparin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subsequent-nursing-care">Subsequent nursing care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subsequent-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Diet—cardiac diet</li>
<li>Patient’s continuous observations for oedema, cyanosis</li>
<li>Exercises—passive exercises first and later active exercises.</li>
<li>Health educate patient on avoidance of the predisposing factors like stopping cigarette smoking, reduce weight, reduce fat diet and salt intake regular exercises, stress management and control and treatment of infections.</li>
<li>Comply with the prescribed medications.</li>
<li>Adhere to cardiac diet.</li>
<li>Have enough rest.</li>
<li>Resumption to work/job or activities.</li>
<li>Return to the clinic or hospital on the appointed review day/date.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Heart failure.</li>
<li>Myocardial infarction.</li>
<li>Stroke.</li>
<li>Kidney failure.</li>
<li>Death.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="conditions-of-haematologic-system-haematologic-disorders">CONDITIONS OF HAEMATOLOGIC SYSTEM (HAEMATOLOGIC DISORDERS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conditions-of-haematologic-system-haematologic-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anaemia">ANAEMIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Refers to the reduction in the amount of red blood cells or haemoglobin or both for the age and sex of the individual</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-and-types-of-anaemia">CAUSES AND TYPES OF ANAEMIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-and-types-of-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Haemorrhagic anaemia (acute or chronic haemorrhagic anaemia)</li>
</ol>
<p>Anaemia due to excess blood loss</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causes-of-acute-blood-loss">Causes of acute blood loss<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-acute-blood-loss" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Severe epistaxis</li>
<li>Injuries/ trauma e.g. RTA, operation</li>
<li>Child birth- APH, PPH</li>
<li>Blood vessel rapture-esophageal varices rupture</li>
<li>Severe hemophilia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causes-of-chronic-blood-loss">Causes of chronic blood loss<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-chronic-blood-loss" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Gastritis-haemoptysis (peptic ulcers</p>
<p>Menstrual flow (menorrhagia)</p>
<p>Haemorrhoids</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Haemolytic anaemia.</li>
</ol>
<p>Occurs due to excess destruction of red blood cells</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Infections- malaria, septicemia, hepatitis</li>
<li>Blood incompatibility during blood transfusion</li>
<li>Congenital haemolytic anaemia like sickle cell patients</li>
<li>Rhesus factor incompatibility</li>
<li>Enzyme deficiencies e.g. G6PD</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Iron deficiency anaemia</li>
</ol>
<p>Ours due to inadequate iron in the body</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Insufficient iron dietary intake</p>
<p>Malabsorption due to chronic diarrhea, inflammatory bowel diseases</p>
<p>Chronic blood loss- in haemorrhoids, GI bleeding, pph</p>
<p>Pregnancy</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-megaloblastic-anaemia">4. Megaloblastic anaemia.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-megaloblastic-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Impaired DNA synthesis which leads to production of large red blood cells (macrocytic)</p>
<p>Folic acid deficiency due to poor nutrition, malabsorption syndrome, drugs (anticancer drugs, oral contraceptives, anti-convulsants), alcohol abuse, hemodialysis</p>
<p>Vitamin B12 (cobalamine) deficiency</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-pernicious-anaemia">5. Pernicious anaemia.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-pernicious-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is due to lack of absorption of vitamin B12 or absence of an intrinsic factor secreted by the parietal cells which results in a decrease in HCl by the stomach.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-aplastic-anaemia">6. Aplastic anaemia.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-aplastic-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Occurs as a result of bone marrow defects (decrease in all blood cell types like RBCs, WBCs and platelets</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unknown-70%</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Drugs like chloramphenicol (it causes bone marrow depression)</li>
<li>Radiations</li>
<li>Chemical agents like insectide, alcohol etc.</li>
<li>Chromosomal alterations</li>
<li>Viral and bacterial infections e.g. hepatitis, TB</li>
<li>Chronic diseases like chronic rheumatoid arthritis, renal failure</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>SICKLE CELL ANAEMIA</li>
</ol>
<p>Occurs due to excess destruction of RBCs due to their abnormal shape (sickle) making them more fragile and prone to breaking down.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-signs-and-symptoms-of-anaemia">General signs and symptoms of anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-signs-and-symptoms-of-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dry skin</li>
<li>Paleness of the mucus membranes, skin, and finger nail beds.</li>
<li>Jaundice</li>
<li>Pruritus due to jaundice</li>
<li>Dizziness, drowsiness</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>General body weakness and fatigue</li>
<li>Rapid pulse and palpitations</li>
<li>Blurred vision</li>
<li>Difficulty in breathing with cyanosis</li>
<li>Anorexia</li>
<li>Oedema of the lower limbs</li>
<li>Chest pain- angina pectoris</li>
<li>Myocardial infarction signs/ symptoms</li>
<li>Restlessness and irritability</li>
<li>Insomnia</li>
<li>Bone pain- in aplastic and sickle cell anaemia</li>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>Signs and symptoms of cardiac failure.</li>
</ul>
<p>Investigations</p>
<ul>
<li>Signs and symptoms (history taking)</li>
<li>Blood for – haemoglobin levels, serum iron and ferritin and iron binding capacity, WBCs, RBCs and platelets, grouping and cross matching, sickle cell test</li>
<li>Bone marrow puncture and biopsy</li>
<li>Gastric juice testing for levels of intrinsic factor</li>
<li>Serum bilirubin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-anaemia">MANAGEMENT OF ANAEMIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Aims</p>
<p>To treat the cause</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>To health educate the patient about anaemia prevention</p>
<p>To prevent complications</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-mild-anaemia">Management of mild anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-mild-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Identify and treat the cause</p>
<p>Educate the patient on diet i.e. Red meat, liver greens leafy vegetables, pork, fish, legumes, eggs, potatoes milk, citrus fruits, strawberries, tomatoes</p>
<p>Oral Haematenics- ferrous sulphate 200-400mg three times a days, folic acid 5mg 2-3 times a day</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-moderate-anaemia">Management of moderate anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-moderate-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Identify and treat the cause e.g. malaria, worms, diarrhea</p>
<p>Diet- rich in iron and folic acid</p>
<p>I.V or I.M iron (interferon) 5mg once a day for 5-10 days, and then later iron tablets</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-severe-anaemia">Management of severe anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-severe-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Admit patient in a medical ward near nurses table in a well-ventilated room</li>
<li>☑ Position- patient is put in a sitting up position in dyspnoea, in shock elevate the foot the bed</li>
<li>☑ Administer oxygen in severe dyspnoea and cyanosis</li>
<li>☑ Observations- vital observation temperature, pulse, respirations and blood pressure. In severe stage (shock) monitor vitals quarter hourly, half hourly then 2 hourly, 4 hourly until the conditions improves. Strictly document the vital observations findings and report the deviations. Observe patient for signs of shock, cyanosis and mental state.</li>
<li>☑ Psychotherapy- reassure patient and patient’s relatives to allay anxiety</li>
<li>☑ Investigations – all the ordered investigations are taken off and taken to the laboratory and the results are brought as soon as they are ready</li>
<li>☑ Patient is prepared for blood transfusion</li>
<li>☑ Blood transfusion is started as soon as blood is ready</li>
<li>☑ After blood transfusion, oral iron tablets are given (ferrous sulphate 200mg 3 times a day)</li>
<li>☑ NOTE: in health unit/ hospital where there is no blood for transfusion and the patient is severe anaemia, iron supplements are given i.e. injection inferno 5mg I.M for 5-10 days or total dose of inferon - 5mg x7 days infused in 500mls of normal saline (35mg in 500mls of normal saline I.V infusion slowly).</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Diet-high protein diet, food rich in iron (as already mentioned), vitamins, plenty of fluids and fruits.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Hygiene- complete bed rest in severely anaemia patients and therefore everything is done for the patient like bed bath, mouth care, regular turning, pressure area care
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Bladder and bowel care-monitor and balance the fluid balance chart and prevent constipation
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Exercise: passive and active exercises
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Advise on discharge;</p>
<p>To eat a well-balanced diet rich in iron, vitamins, proteins and vegetables</p>
<p>To take the drugs as prescribed.</p>
<p>To come back for review on the appointed date</p>
<p>To have enough rest.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-anaemia">Prevention of anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Health educate on:</li>
<li>Sanitation (personal and environmental sanitation). The importance of having a pit latrine</li>
<li>Eat a well-balanced diet</li>
<li>Ensure proper weaning of children to avoid nutrition anaemia</li>
<li>Deworming children/ and adults against worms.</li>
<li>Child spacing to avoid excess blood loss in delivery</li>
<li>Proper management of labor</li>
<li>Regular medical check-up for any abnormalities</li>
<li>Patients with sickle cell must be prevented from any infections and other triggering factors</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-anaemia">Complications of anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain damage</li>
<li>Respiratory failure</li>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Low resistance to infections</li>
<li>Heart failure</li>
<li>Malnutrition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leukaemia">LEUKAEMIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leukaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a term that describes a group of malignant disorders affecting the blood and blood forming tissues of the bone marrow characterized by excessive multiplication of WBCs.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>41</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>It affects bone marrow, lymph system and spleen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The exact cause of Leukemia is not known.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors-to-leukemia">Predisposing factors to leukemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-to-leukemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetic predisposition</li>
<li>Chemical agents like benzene</li>
<li>Chemotherapeutic agents like alkylating agents</li>
<li>Virus</li>
<li>Radiation</li>
<li>Immunological deficiencies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-leukemia">Signs and symptoms of Leukemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-leukemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fevers</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Loss of weight</li>
<li>Bleeding tendencies</li>
<li>Frequent infections</li>
<li>Fatigue and general body weakness</li>
<li>Mouth ulcers</li>
<li>Bone, joint and abdominal pain</li>
<li>Lymphadenopathy</li>
<li>Hepato-splenomegaly</li>
<li>Headache</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-leukemia">Types of Leukemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-leukemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Acute myelogenous leukemia (AML)
Characterized by uncontrolled proliferation of myeloblasts
(Hyperplasia of bone marrow and spleen)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acute lymphocytic leukemia (ALL)
Characterized by proliferation of lymphocytes in the bone marrow</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chronic Myelogenous Leukemia (CML)
Due to excessive development of mature meoplastic granulocytes in the bone marrow</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chronic Lymphocytic Leukemia
Caused by production and accumulation of functionally inactive but long-lived, mature – appearing lymphocytes.</p>
</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations-and-diagnosis">Investigations and Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations-and-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Bleed for WBS, Hb levels, Haematocut</li>
<li>Bone marrow aspiration and examination</li>
<li>Lumbar puncture for CSF</li>
<li>CT scan</li>
<li>Bone/ skeletal x-ray</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Aims of management</p>
<ul>
<li>To destroy leukaemia cells</li>
<li>To prolong life</li>
</ul>
<p>The treatment is directed to giving drugs that can temporarily destroy the leukaemia cells and therefore prolong life of a patient.</p>
<p>Blood transfusion and placement of blood cells may relieve symptoms</p>
<p>Administration of cytotoxic drugs like – cyclophosphamide, mrthotrexate, Vincistne IV 1.4mg, Doxorubicin</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="steroids">Steroids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steroids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Prednisone
Antibiotics to treat any infections</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptomatic-treatment">Symptomatic treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptomatic-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pain relievers – strong analgesics</li>
<li>Blood transfusion in anaemia</li>
<li>Tepid sponge if there is fever</li>
<li>Psychotherapy – encourage patient to live a normal life</li>
<li>Health educate patient on:-</li>
<li>The complexity and chronicity of the disease</li>
<li>The need to have a combination / variety of cytotoxic drugs</li>
<li>The importance of drug compliance</li>
<li>The possible side effects especially after starting the cytotoxic drugs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-rxs">Other RXs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-rxs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Bone marrow and stem cell transplant</li>
<li>Radiotherapy</li>
</ul>
<p>43</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="coagulation-disorders">COAGULATION DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coagulation-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="haemophilia">HAEMOPHILIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemophilia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a sex-linked recessive genetic disorder caused by defective or deficient coagulation factor (it is blood disorder). It occurs only in males and transmitted by females (i.e. females are carriers and males are the sicklers/ sufferers).</p>
<p>There are two forms of Haemophilia</p>
<p>I. Haemophilia A (classic Haemophilia)</p>
<p>Due to factor VIII deficiency</p>
<p>It is the most common one making up 80% of all cases</p>
<p>II. Haemophilia B (Christmas disease)</p>
<p>Due to factor IX deficiency)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-haemophilia">Signs and symptoms of Haemophilia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-haemophilia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Slow, persistent and prolonged bleeding from minor trauma and small cuts</li>
<li>Delayed bleeding after minor injuries/ surgery</li>
<li>Uncontrollable haemorrhage after dental extraction.</li>
<li>Irritation of the gum with a hard brittle tooth brush</li>
<li>Epistaxis especially after a blow to the face</li>
<li>Haematuria</li>
<li>GI bleeding from ulcers and gastritis</li>
<li>Ecchymosis and subcutaneous haematoma</li>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Parasthesia and paralysis</li>
<li>Bleeding into joints (haemarthrosis) which may lead to joint deformity causing crippling in the knees, elbow, hip shoulders and ankles.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations">INVESTIGATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>History taking</li>
<li>Signs and symptoms</li>
<li>Blood for haemoglobin levels. Grouping and cross matching.</li>
<li>Blood for clotting factors – VII, IX, XI or XII</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hiv-aids">HIV/AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hiv-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>x-ray of the joints (skeletal x-ray)</li>
<li>Prothrombin and bleeding time</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aims">Aims<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>To raise the levels of clotting factors</li>
<li>To prevent and treat bleeding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="immediate-intervention">Immediate intervention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immediate-intervention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Stop the topical bleeding as quickly as possible by applying direct pressure, ice packs. Packing the area with topical haemostatic agents like thrombin, Adrenaline.</li>
<li>Blood transfusion with fresh frozen plasma.</li>
<li>Administer the specific coagulation factor (Anti Haemophilia factor – AHF) in order to raise the patient’s level of the deficient coagulation factor. Antifibrinolytics like traxemic acid is given.</li>
<li>In Haemarthrosis- ensure complete bed rest to prevent crippling deformities. Apply a bed cradle. Apply ice compresses onto the painful joints. Administer analgesics like codeine, Morphine and then PCM to relieve pain (DONOT administer ASPIRIN).</li>
<li>Reassure patient and patient’s relatives to allay anxiety.</li>
<li>Exercises – When bleeding stops, encourage mobilization of the affected areas through range of motion exercises and physical therapy (Both passive and active exercises).</li>
<li>Any complications of haemorrhage like shock, infections, should be promptly and appropriately treated.</li>
<li>Hygiene – specifically oral hygiene to avoid brushing using very hard – rough tooth brushes, to avoid eating irritating foods and hard foods and irritating chemicals.</li>
<li>Diet – Encourage a highly nutritious diet like plenty of proteins/ Albumin, vitamins, fresh fruits and juicy and calcium containing foods. Plenty of oral fluids.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Prevention of severe and prolonged bleeding in Haemophilia</p>
<ul>
<li>To health educate the patient and relatives about the course of the disease.</li>
<li>To avoid trauma as a result of fighting (blows to face)</li>
<li>To participate only in non- contact games like golf, tennis</li>
<li>To wear gloves (woolen gloves) when doing household chores to prevent cuts, abrasions from knives, hummers or other fools.</li>
</ul>

Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Before any surgery, the patient should be given an infusion of plasma or blood transfused.</li>
<li>If a patient is to receive an injection, a small needle should be used.</li>
<li>All patients with hemophilia must/ should be supported psychologically and socially for example</li>
<li>School going children – Their teachers should explain to avoid beating them at school with sharp objects.</li>
<li>Working people – Their employers must be explained to</li>
<li>To seek medical attention in case of any severe prolonged bleeding.</li>
<li>To comply with the treatment and preventive measures as instructed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sickle-cell-disease">SICKLE CELL DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sickle-cell-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Refers to a group of inherited, autosomal, recessive disorders characterized by the presence of an abnormal form of haemoglobin in the erythrocyte</p>
<p>The abnormal haemoglobin is called haemoglobin sickle (Hbs)</p>
<p>Individuals who inherit the Hbs from one parent have sickle cell trait (HbAS) and are carriers.</p>
<p>Those who inherit the Hbs from both parents have sickle cell disease Hbss and are sicklers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Haemoglobin sickle or sickle cells come as a result of substitution of valine for glutamic acid on the globin chain of haemoglobin.</p>
<p>The sickling episodes are commonly triggered by: - hypoxia caused by viral or bacterial infections, extreme coldness, and severe dehydration.</p>
<p>The sickled RBCs become rigid and take on an elongated, crescent shape. These sickled cells cannot easily pass through capillaries or other small vessels and cause vascular occlusion leading to acute or chronic tissue injury thus haemostasis causing sickle cell crisis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-sickle-cell-crisis">Types of sickle cell crisis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-sickle-cell-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="thrombotic-crisis">Thrombotic crisis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thrombotic-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Occurs due to clotting of blood in the tinny blood vessels like capillaries causing stasis of blood</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Other parts of the body will have less blood causing severe pain in the peripheral joints and muscles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="haemolytic-crisis">Haemolytic crisis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemolytic-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is due to excess break down of RBCs like in malaria, severe jaundice etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sequestration-crisis-splenic-sequestration">Sequestration crisis (splenic sequestration)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sequestration-crisis-splenic-sequestration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The vaso-occlusion produces an acute painful enlargement of the spleen. There is splenic pooling of the RBCs and Hypovolaemia leading to circulatory collapse and death in some patients. Hepatic pooling also occurs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aplastic-crisis">Aplastic crisis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aplastic-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Here the bone marrow is affected and cannot manufacture RBCs resulting into a rapid fall in haemoglobin with no reticulocytes in the peripheral blood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incidences">Incidences<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incidences" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Starts from 6 months and above</li>
<li>It affects both sexes</li>
<li>It's common in tropics</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: both parents have to be carriers to release sickled RBCs.i.e.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251215-564e48de.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>AA- Normal
AS- Carrier
SS- Sickler</p>
<p>Signs and symptoms of sickle cell disease</p>
<p>This document is available on
47
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Fevers due to infections</li>
<li>General malaise</li>
<li>Jaundice due to excessive hemolysis</li>
<li>Sharp severe chest pain due to infection, fat embolism, pulmonary infarction.</li>
<li>Joint and bone pain due to clumping of RBCs in the bone marrow they try to produce many RBCs.</li>
<li>Acute pain in the hands and feet due to vaso-occlusion</li>
<li>Splenomegaly and hepatomegaly</li>
<li>Severe anaemia due to splenic sequestration, hemolysis and bone marrow aplasia</li>
<li>Growth and development failure due to poor bone development</li>
<li>Bossing of the head(skull) due to poor flat bone development</li>
<li>Low resistance to infections. Acute abdominal pain due to vaso-occlusion</li>
<li>Cholelithiasis due to chronic hemolysis</li>
<li>Myocardial infarction</li>
<li>Cardiomegaly with cardiac arrhythmias altered conscious levels with coma due to cerebral infarction and haemorrhage.</li>
<li>Priapism- painful persistent erection due to occlusion and stasis of blood in the erectile organ and this may lead to impotence</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Severe headache</li>
<li>Prominent eyes with retinal haemorrhage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>History taking-sickle cells in parents</li>
<li>Clinical presentation</li>
<li>Blood work-haemoglobin levels, grouping and cross matching. Blood for CBC, clotting time, B/S for malaria</li>
<li>Serum bilirubin</li>
<li>HB electrophoresis</li>
<li>Skeletal x-rays to rule out bone and deformities and flattening</li>
<li>Sickle cell test</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-sickle-cell-disease">MANAGEMENT OF SICKLE CELL DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-sickle-cell-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aims">Aims<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>To alleviate the symptoms</li>
<li>To rest the patient</li>
<li>To prevent complications</li>
</ul>
<p>There is no specific treatment; instead all the triggering factors must be prevented like</p>
<p>To avoid high altitudes</p>
<p>To avoid dehydration – ensure adequate hydration</p>
<p>Treat any infections</p>
<p>To avoid stress</p>
<p>To avoid extreme coldness</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="in-sickle-cell-anaemia-or-sickle-cell-crisis">In sickle cell anaemia or sickle cell crisis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#in-sickle-cell-anaemia-or-sickle-cell-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit</li>
<li>Ensure complete bed rest</li>
<li>Observations – vital observations, temperature, pulse, respirations, and blood pressure 4 hourly</li>
<li>Relieve pain – morphine 5-15 mg or Pethidine 25-100 mg whenever necessary (PRN), paracetamol 250 mg – 1 g 3 times a day</li>
<li>Administer oxygen to treat hypoxia and control sickling</li>
<li>Intravenous fluids and or plenty of oral fluids to reduce blood viscosity</li>
<li>Infection control and prevention.</li>
<li>Drug therapy:</li>
<li>Antibiotics for any infections like penicillins</li>
<li>Antimalarial like Fansidar</li>
<li>Multivitamins to boost the immunity and improve appetite</li>
<li>Analgesics – strong analgesics first then mild analgesics as listed above</li>
<li>Sedatives to promote rest</li>
<li>Blood transfusion in severe anaemia, aplastic crisis and other crisis</li>
<li>Haematenics – folic acid. DONOT GIVE FERROUS SULPHATE</li>
<li>Anti-sickling agents like hydroxyurea</li>
<li>Anticoagulants in thrombotic crisis</li>
<li>Erythropoietin therapy</li>
<li>Bone marrow transplantation – it is the only treatment that can cure some patients with SCD</li>
<li>Diet – plenty of fluids</li>
<li>Avoid acidic and spiced food</li>
<li>Give high protein diet, plenty of vitamins, food containing folic acid, roughages.</li>
<li>Bladder and bowel care</li>
<li>Hygiene – daily bathing, mouth care, regular turning and pressure area care</li>
<li>Prophylactic treatment – Fansidar (antimalarial), Haematenics to prevent anaemia, dewormers</li>
</ul>
